  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0c00f6c4-a2c1-4073-9572-d2708af45eb7'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer4083683215101957905"><i>Librarian's Note: Alternate cover for this ISBN can be found <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5972886-forward-the-foundation' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a></i><br/><br/>Here, from a grand master of science fiction, is the long awaited final novel of the greatest series ever told.   <span id="freeText4083683215101957905" style="display:none"><i>Librarian's Note: Alternate cover for this ISBN can be found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5972886-forward-the-foundation" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></i><br /><br />Here, from a grand master of science fiction, is the long awaited final novel of the greatest series ever told. Completed just before his death, <i>Forward The Foundation</i> is the crowning achievement of a great writer's life, a stirring testament to the creative genius of Isaac Asimov. <br /><br />As Hari Seldon struggles to perfect his revolutionary theory of psychohistory and ensure a place for humanity among the stars, the great Galactic Empire totters on the brink of apocalyptic collapse. Caught in the maelstrom are Seldon and all he holds dear, pawns in the struggle for dominance. Whoever can control Seldon will control psychohistory—and with it the future of the Galaxy. <br /><br />Among those seeking to turn psychohistory into the greatest weapon known to man are a populist political demagogue, the weak-willed Emperor Cleon I, and a ruthless militaristic general. In his last act of service to humankind, Hari Seldon must somehow save his life's work from their grasp as he searches for is true heirs—a search the begins with his own granddaughter and the dream of a new Foundation.</span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788804418054" href="/book/show/9646838-fondazione-anno-zero">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1581170866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7476101386555813109">ENGLISH (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76679.Forward_the_Foundation__Foundation_Prequel__2_' title='Forward the Foundation (Foundation Prequel #2) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Forward the Foundation</a>) / ITALIANO<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Though <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov' title='Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Isaac Asimov</a> was a remarkable scientific divulgator, we cannot forget that one of the most fascinating cycles of ancient science fiction, i.e. the Foundation series, was born from his pen. Thanks to his work, Asimov can be rightly considered one of the earliest and most direct inspiring of Hari Seldon, the founder of Psichohistory, the science of human behavior reduced to mathematical equations" ENCYCLOPEDIA GALACTICA</i>
</blockquote> Second prequel of the F</span>
  <span id="freeText7476101386555813109" style="display:none">ENGLISH (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76679.Forward_the_Foundation__Foundation_Prequel__2_" title="Forward the Foundation (Foundation Prequel #2) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Forward the Foundation</a>) / ITALIANO<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Though <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Isaac Asimov</a> was a remarkable scientific divulgator, we cannot forget that one of the most fascinating cycles of ancient science fiction, i.e. the Foundation series, was born from his pen. Thanks to his work, Asimov can be rightly considered one of the earliest and most direct inspiring of Hari Seldon, the founder of Psichohistory, the science of human behavior reduced to mathematical equations" ENCYCLOPEDIA GALACTICA</i>
</blockquote> Second prequel of the Foundation series, the novel takes place on Trantor 8 years after the first prequel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30013.Prelude_to_Foundation" title="Prelude to Foundation by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Prelude to Foundation</a>. The main character is once again Hari Seldon, committed to the development and practical application of Psychohistory. Despite the time frame of the narration is quite long (basically the entire Seldon's life is narrated in this book), the rythm of events is intensive, and twists and turns are not missing. However, I would now like to make a clarification: my judgment is definitely not objective, 'cause I love Asimov's spying fantasy science and his fascinating theory of spatial colonization.<p>Vote: 8</p><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497964050i/23073009._SX540_.jpg" width="420" height="316" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Benchè <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16667.Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Isaac Asimov</a> sia stato un notevole divulgatore scientifico, non si può dimenticare che uno dei cicli più affascinanti della fantascienza antica, il ciclo delle fondazioni, sia nato dalla sua penna. Grazie alla sua opera, può essere di diritto annoverato tra i primi e più diretti ispiratori di Hari Seldon, il padre fondatore della psicostoria, la scienza del comportamento umano ridotto ad equazioni matematiche" ENCICLOPEDIA GALATTICA</i>
</blockquote>Secondo prequel al ciclo delle fondazioni vero e proprio, il romanzo si svolge su Trantor a partire da 8 anni dopo il primo prequel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10314009.Preludio_alla_Fondazione" title="Preludio alla Fondazione by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Preludio alla Fondazione</a>. Il protagonista è ancora una volta Hari Seldon, impegnato nello sviluppo e nell'applicazione pratica della Psicostoria. Nonostante l'arco temporale della narrazione sia piuttosto lungo, essendo spalmato per tutta la rimanente vita di Seldon, il ritmo rimane discretamente serrato, e non mancano i colpi di scena. Occorre però fare una precisazione: il mio giudizio è assolutamente non obiettivo, essendo un amante dello spionaggio fantascientifico di Asimov e della sua affascinante teoria della colonizzazione spaziale.<p>Voto: 8.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="7476101386555813109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2762686493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2762686493" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2762686493?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2762686493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer92143696340770181">Finally! The last published Foundation book, written by Asimov (a few more titles written by other authors were published subsequently). <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/927628455' rel='nofollow noopener'>My review of the first Foundation book</a> was posted in 2014, as I write it is March 2019, so I feel a nice sense of accomplishment for completing a series review five years in the making. <br/><br/><i>Forward the Foundation</i> is the second prequel to the classic original <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46654.The_Foundation_Trilogy__Foundation___1_3_' title='The Foundation Trilogy (Foundation, #1-3) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'> Foundation Trilogy</a> (that makes it a sequel to a prequel! <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30013.Prelude_to_Foundation' title='Prelude to Foundation by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'> Prelude to Foundation</a> that is). It is set on Tran</span>
  <span id="freeText92143696340770181" style="display:none">Finally! The last published Foundation book, written by Asimov (a few more titles written by other authors were published subsequently). <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/927628455" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of the first Foundation book</a> was posted in 2014, as I write it is March 2019, so I feel a nice sense of accomplishment for completing a series review five years in the making. <br><br><i>Forward the Foundation</i> is the second prequel to the classic original <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46654.The_Foundation_Trilogy__Foundation___1_3_" title="The Foundation Trilogy (Foundation, #1-3) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener"> Foundation Trilogy</a> (that makes it a sequel to a prequel! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30013.Prelude_to_Foundation" title="Prelude to Foundation by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener"> Prelude to Foundation</a> that is). It is set on Trantor, the governing planet of the Galactic Empire, eight years after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30013.Prelude_to_Foundation" title="Prelude to Foundation by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener"> Prelude to Foundation</a>. “Prelude” tells the story of Hari Seldon, the founder of the Foundation, as a young man, and the development of “psychohistory”, a predictive science for computing monumental events on a planetary or even galactic scale. <br><i>“It’s a mathematical way of analyzing human society that ends by predicting the future.”</i><br>At the beginning of <i>Forward the Foundation</i> Hari Seldon is 60-year-old, and the novel tells the story of the last ten years of his life, as he struggles to put the Foundation together. As his psychohistory predicts, the Empire is deteriorating and beginning to fall. Seldon’s mission in life is to minimize the duration of the dark age that will follow this fall, with the Foundation as the nucleus of a new empire. He is aided by his wife, Dors, who seems to possess some superhuman abilities, his adopted son and granddaughter, who have some uncanny mental abilities and several other colorful characters.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1553568755i/27265231._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Who is this bloke from the book cover of several editions? No idea, too young to be Seldon! That black box is probably the “Prime Radiant”, but WTF is he doing with it?</i><br><br><i>Forward the Foundation</i> is pretty great for fans of this classic sci-fi series, it fills out details of things mentioned in the original Foundation Trilogy. However, I personally have some doubts about reading the entire series in chronological order instead of the publication order. The original trilogy, from the 50s, is comprised of three rather short novels, very tightly written and often quite thrilling. This is the case with most of the best Golden Age sci-fi books, they tend to be great stories economically told. I think that anyone new to the Foundation books would be better off reading the trilogy first simply because they are just more fun and exciting. The extra details from the prequels are not really needed to follow the trilogy’s narrative. That said, Asimov himself recommended reading in the chronological order so you may want to ignore me completely!<br><br>In and of itself though <i>Forward the Foundation</i> is a solid novel, rather leisurely paced, as is the case of the later Asimov works from the 80s and 90s. Asimov seems to more interested in pondering and exploring ideas than telling gripping, fast-paced stories. The characterization tends to be better in these later novels, the main characters, including the smart villains, have more depth to them, the plot structure tends to be more intricate and complex. The stylistic changes are only natural as Asimov matured and changed, readers who prefer his 50s writing style have plenty of titles they can choose from as this was his most prolific period. In any case, his 80s and 90s books are interesting and very readable and I enjoy them. As a longtime fan of his books, I feel a little nostalgic, like reaching the end of an era. I don’t really feel inclined to read the subsequently published Foundation books by other authors, what I would rather do is go back to reread his early robots and empire books. Whatever order you want to read the Foundation series is up to you, I am happy with my reading order and I love the series in general.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479114831i/21148337.jpg" alt="sapce line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>Notes:</b><br>• A little spoiler discussion, only read this if you have already read this book (or if you enjoy being contrary). Here goes: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Towards the end Seldon is working hard to set up the Second Foundation, the community to be made up of people with mental powers, basically telepathy and mind control. The usage of mind control is presented as a wonderful tool to achieve Seldon’s goals. I find this very odd, it is as if Asimov never considered that mind control is actually very dangerous, and deprives people of free will. He even depicted this danger with “The Mule” in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29581.Foundation_and_Empire__Foundation__2_" title="Foundation and Empire (Foundation #2) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener"> Foundation and Empire</a>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>• In a previous Foundation book review (I forget which one) I mentioned that there are no aliens in the Foundation series. This is kind of correct, but there is Gaia in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76683.Foundation_s_Edge__Foundation__4_" title="Foundation's Edge (Foundation #4) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener"> Foundation's Edge</a> which is a non-human sentient entity. See Wastrel's comment, in message #5 under the review, for more details.<br><br>*<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foundation_series#Chronological_reading_order" rel="nofollow noopener">Chronological reading order</a>. You don't have to read every single one of them! Some of them barely add anything to the series’ narrative.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="92143696340770181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438577050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14575449946070280896">Forward the Foundation (Foundation (Publication Order) #7), Isaac Asimov<br/>Forward the Foundation is a novel by American writer Isaac Asimov, published posthumously in 1993. Continues the chronicles of the life of Hari Seldon, first begun in Prelude to Foundation. The story takes place on Trantor, and begins eight years after the events of Prelude to Foundation. It depicts how Seldon develops his theory of psychohistory from hypothetical concept to practical application. In the latter years of the </span>
  <span id="freeText14575449946070280896" style="display:none">Forward the Foundation (Foundation (Publication Order) #7), Isaac Asimov<br />Forward the Foundation is a novel by American writer Isaac Asimov, published posthumously in 1993. Continues the chronicles of the life of Hari Seldon, first begun in Prelude to Foundation. The story takes place on Trantor, and begins eight years after the events of Prelude to Foundation. It depicts how Seldon develops his theory of psychohistory from hypothetical concept to practical application. In the latter years of the reign of Emperor Cleon I, Seldon is dragged into the world of galactic politics as Cleon's somewhat unwilling First Minister, after the resignation of his predecessor, Eto Demerzel (whom Seldon knows as the robot R. Daneel Olivaw). After the Emperor is assassinated, a military junta takes over for a disastrous decade. Seldon steps down from his government position and resumes leadership of the psychohistory project. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 1999 میلادی<br />عنوان: پ‍ی‍ش‍ب‍رد ب‍ن‍ی‍اد ک‍ه‍ک‍ش‍ان‍ی‌؛ نویسنده: آی‍زاک‌ آس‍ی‍م‍وف‌؛ مت‍رج‍م: پ‍ی‍م‍ان‌ اس‍م‍اع‍ی‍ل‍ی‍ان‌‌خ‍ام‍ن‍ه؛ تهران، بنیاد مستصعفان، چاپ و نشر بنیاد، 1376، در 471 ص؛ شابک: 9646333052؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان روسی تبار آمریکایی - سده 20 م<br /><br />کتاب «پیشبرد بنیاد کهکشانی»، جزوی از مجموعه‌ «بنیاد» هفت جلدی از «آیزاک آسیموف» است که مشهورترین مجموعه‌ علمی-تخیلی خوانده شده‌ است. داستان این مجموعه به ترتیب زمان انتشار پیش نمی‌رود، بلکه «آسیموف» نخست جلدهای سوم با عنوان (بنیاد)، چهارم با عنوان (بنیاد و امپراطوری) و پنجم با عنوان (بنیاد دوم) را نوشتند و سپس با وقفه‌ ای طولانی مدت، جلدهای ششم با عنوان (لبه‌ بنیاد) و هفتم را به مجموعه افزودند. ا. شربیانی<br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385247931" href="/book/show/415995.Forward_the_Foundation">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Eric by: </span>
      Those reading the entire series

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/351034-eric?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer568865810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7383494205927202778">The critical reviews of this book are astounding.<br/>"The breathtaking conclusion to the greatest science fiction epic of all time" is a strange thing to say about a book that serves as a second prequel...and not the last of the series either. <br/><br/>"The Foundation series has enthralled readers for more than 40 years, and this work is a dramatic climax." Again, for a prequel, and, frankly, it's not particularly dramatic.<br/><br/>"A moving valedictory performance..." which means...I'm not sure what...<br/><br/>Little known f</span>
  <span id="freeText7383494205927202778" style="display:none">The critical reviews of this book are astounding.<br />"The breathtaking conclusion to the greatest science fiction epic of all time" is a strange thing to say about a book that serves as a second prequel...and not the last of the series either. <br /><br />"The Foundation series has enthralled readers for more than 40 years, and this work is a dramatic climax." Again, for a prequel, and, frankly, it's not particularly dramatic.<br /><br />"A moving valedictory performance..." which means...I'm not sure what...<br /><br />Little known fact: Asimov generated character names using a random number generator. <br /><br />That said, the book isn't terrible. I find it to be a little pointless and increasingly implausible. But it fits into the series, and the series may well be the "greatest science fiction epic of all time". If it is, it's not because of the prose, the drama, or the characters. It's because of the concepts. The Universe in which stories occur is a magnificent tapestry. Even if the stories themselves fall short of this standard time after time, the occasional glimpses of Asimov's Universe make it worth the read, regardless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7383494205927202778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1862985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1862985" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/125045-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1862985?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/125045-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1862985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer798611542961700903">"Forward the Foundation", Asimov's last novel (written just before his death, published just after), suffers from all the problems of "Prelude to Foundation" only magnified tenfold. Once again, Hari Seldon is transmogrified into an action hero to save the crisis of the day in a prequel to the older and vastly superior Foundation novels. Unlike Prelude, however, there's not enough going on outside the short-term arc to make this one worthwhile. It's just plain silly. Part of what makes the Founda</span>
  <span id="freeText798611542961700903" style="display:none">"Forward the Foundation", Asimov's last novel (written just before his death, published just after), suffers from all the problems of "Prelude to Foundation" only magnified tenfold. Once again, Hari Seldon is transmogrified into an action hero to save the crisis of the day in a prequel to the older and vastly superior Foundation novels. Unlike Prelude, however, there's not enough going on outside the short-term arc to make this one worthwhile. It's just plain silly. Part of what makes the Foundation stories so great is their ability to both offer a good story and present the idea that the individual events pale in significance to the overarching history that Seldon has planned. "Forward the Foundation" accomplishes neither.</span>
  <a data-text-id="798611542961700903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer499769109901348969">Varies from not bad to pretty good. It almost feels more like a trio of connected novellas than one cohesive novel, which is not necessarily a bad thing. But for the most part, the sequences of events seem a little too convenient.   <span id="freeText499769109901348969" style="display:none">Varies from not bad to pretty good. It almost feels more like a trio of connected novellas than one cohesive novel, which is not necessarily a bad thing. But for the most part, the sequences of events seem a little too convenient. That said, the characters are pretty decent, and the female characters are significantly more capable and well-rounded than I'm used to seeing from these Great Old SF Masters, and indeed from some of Asimov's own older works. Maybe I would have appreciated it more if I'd read the Foundation books in publication order instead of internal chronological order, but that's not how I approached it.</span>

<div id="review_2000088145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2000088145" />
    <a title="Buck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9120555-buck"><img alt="Buck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465429605p2/9120555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2000088145?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Buck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Buck" href="/user/show/9120555-buck">Buck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio 9780307970626" href="/book/show/13134208-forward-the-foundation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9120555-buck?shelf=wwend-2017">wwend-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9120555-buck?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9120555-buck?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2000088145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11932019227004536510">When I was young, Isaac Asimov was my favorite author. I read a lot of his books, science fiction and science fact, novels and short stories. I had decided that his short stories were better than his novels, that his novels were written like long short stories. I have forgotten most of what I had read of his books and in recent years I've been rereading.<br/><br/>Forward the Foundation was written after my youthful fanship. It does sort of confirm my early opinion. Asimov is not great at dialog. It is sti</span>
  <span id="freeText11932019227004536510" style="display:none">When I was young, Isaac Asimov was my favorite author. I read a lot of his books, science fiction and science fact, novels and short stories. I had decided that his short stories were better than his novels, that his novels were written like long short stories. I have forgotten most of what I had read of his books and in recent years I've been rereading.<br /><br />Forward the Foundation was written after my youthful fanship. It does sort of confirm my early opinion. Asimov is not great at dialog. It is stiff, sometimes stodgy, and weak on inflection and nuance. In the audio book that I just heard, I think this was made to seem even more so by the narrator, Larry McKeever. R Daneel Olivaw made an appearance in Forward the Foundation, as he does in several of Asimov's late works. I think Asmiov's dialog style suits Daneel, being a robot.<br /><br />Hari Seldon, the developer of psycho-history, the basis of the Foundation series, is pretty much the same character as Elijah Baley, in the Robot series, and Golan Trevize in the Foundation sequels, and probably most of Asimov's leading characters in other novels.<br /><br />So, having denigrated the object of my early SF literary admiration, let me say that I haven't read anything of Asimov's that isn't pretty good. (Which I can't say of his contemporaries I also admire, Philip K Dick and Robert A Heinlein, both of whom have writen a couple of dogs.) Forward the Foundation is good old fashioned Sci-Fi and well worth the read, especially in the context of the Foundation Trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11932019227004536510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446386938?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Davyne DeSye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Davyne DeSye" href="/user/show/49054501-davyne-desye">Davyne DeSye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446386938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18223118939179202264">This is the perfect book to go between the first prequel to Foundation (Prelude to Foundation) and Foundation itself!<br/><br/>Of course, having read Foundation first (decades ago), it is difficult for me to look at this book in the same way a reader might who has not read Foundation first – I was constantly (and pleasantly) comparing the thought processes and younger life of the incomparable Hari Seldon in this book to the vision we are given of Seldon in Foundation, when he is established as an old and </span>
  <span id="freeText18223118939179202264" style="display:none">This is the perfect book to go between the first prequel to Foundation (Prelude to Foundation) and Foundation itself!<br /><br />Of course, having read Foundation first (decades ago), it is difficult for me to look at this book in the same way a reader might who has not read Foundation first – I was constantly (and pleasantly) comparing the thought processes and younger life of the incomparable Hari Seldon in this book to the vision we are given of Seldon in Foundation, when he is established as an old and very wise demigod and thorough planner of human civilization for the next millennia. <br /><br />The story is told (sort of) in the form of four novellas and a short story… which, of course, tie together seamlessly. I say this because the novel is, in fact, broken into five parts, with each part dealing with a new decade of Seldon’s life (his 40s, 50s, 60s, 70s and 80s). Each decade sees Seldon having to deal with a new crisis and making new headway on his important psychohistory project (the statistical ability to predict the future). So, in this book we see how the “concept” of psychohistory (which is all that Seldon has in the previous book) develops into the finely-tuned instrument that is in use in Foundation.<br /><br />The other thing that struck me with this book is Seldon’s own inner thought processes as he ages. In his 40s, he has the inevitable “I’m getting old” that (in my experience) few 40-year-olds seem to escape. As the decades pass, he questions whether he really is up to the job mentally of continuing his research – against all evidence to the contrary and the beliefs of his colleagues, friends and family. Asimov manages to present this grinding down of self-confidence in a very real way. Most interestingly though, is the philosophic way Seldon accepts his old age and predicted death toward the end: A not-unhappy looking back on his life, appreciating his time with people he has loved, pondering whether he could or should have done things differently, and an acceptance that he is going to die. I think the reason this aspect of the book struck me as being so genuine is because Asimov finished this book just shortly before his own death. In a way, I could “feel” him looking back through his own decades and the different challenges he faced along the way. I could imagine him at least trying to face his own impending death with the same equanimity that Seldon faced his. (I hope he succeeded.)<br /><br />Overall, this was an extremely well done building up of the legend of Hari Seldon that both enriches and humanizes the character we come to love in Foundation. And I am now so excited to delve into Foundation!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18223118939179202264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_300160859" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300160859" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5860462-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382495111p2/5860462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300160859?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/5860462-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385247931" href="/book/show/415995.Forward_the_Foundation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300160859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12275963097929018407">This was the last novel Isaac Asimov completed before his death in 1992, and it is pervaded by an undercurrent of mortality. Not only does this volume tie up most of the remaining loose ends in the sporadic Foundation series, but by focusing on the latter half of Hari Seldon's life, it provides Asimov with a platform for expressing his own views on growing older.<br/><br/>There is a very clear progression in Asimov's writing style over the years. Although he never entirely overcame his fundamental geekine</span>
  <span id="freeText12275963097929018407" style="display:none">This was the last novel Isaac Asimov completed before his death in 1992, and it is pervaded by an undercurrent of mortality. Not only does this volume tie up most of the remaining loose ends in the sporadic Foundation series, but by focusing on the latter half of Hari Seldon's life, it provides Asimov with a platform for expressing his own views on growing older.<br /><br />There is a very clear progression in Asimov's writing style over the years. Although he never entirely overcame his fundamental geekiness, his style did become considerably more relaxed, less wooden with the passing of years, particularly with regard to characterization and dialogue. And, truth be told, in Asimov's case, even the geekiness holds a certain charm: apart from the characters, the plot, or the specifics of any given book, we, the readers, feel as if the author values our time, treats us well, and never talks down to us. Asimov's voice is that of a friend, and it has been missed in the intervening years.<br /><br />Fans might question the need for what amounts to a second prequel to the Foundation trilogy, but Asimov supplies more than enough by way of the unexpected to both maintain the reader's interest and remain relevant to the larger overall story arc. This is not merely an excuse for an old man to muse in third person about the approach of death. That was just a side benefit of writing this story, and it is perhaps part of his genius that he devised a story that allows for both without sacrificing either.<br /><br />How ironic, when reading Asimov's works, to realize that he did not live long enough to see the rise of the Internet or the construction of the International Space Station. Most personal computers were still running under DOS. Facebook and Twitter were decades in the future. In the end, however, as played out in the book's final scene, Asimov's regrets as he approached the end of his life had less to do with what the future might have held than with the indelible past.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12275963097929018407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11923113705501389798">This was a great, if depressing, way to finish up the Foundation series (if read in published rather than chronological order, obviously). Not only did Asimov continue to improve on writing semi-realistically flawed characters, he also managed to start drawing this reader far more emotional perspectives than before (though I don't think he's really tried to do that before in this series, at least).<br/><br/>Most importantly to me, this book finally tied up one of the loose ends that had been nagging me si</span>
  <span id="freeText11923113705501389798" style="display:none">This was a great, if depressing, way to finish up the Foundation series (if read in published rather than chronological order, obviously). Not only did Asimov continue to improve on writing semi-realistically flawed characters, he also managed to start drawing this reader far more emotional perspectives than before (though I don't think he's really tried to do that before in this series, at least).<br /><br />Most importantly to me, this book finally tied up one of the loose ends that had been nagging me since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29580.Second_Foundation__Foundation__3_" title="Second Foundation (Foundation #3) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener"> Second Foundation</a>: that psychohistorians had somehow gone from a math that couldn't address individuals to a mental ability that only worked on individuals, even while they're math still couldn't venture there. It took four books to get there, but that seemingly large incongruity was finally resolved, and fairly satisfactorily too, allaying the last of my major quips with the series (aside from it not showing Seldon's or Eto's plan coming to fruition).</span>

<div id="review_1617169310" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1617169310" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39746437-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1617169310?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/39746437-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/5972886-forward-the-foundation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1617169310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1800928112150898618">Let me start out by saying DO NOT READ THIS BEFORE THE ORIGINAL TRILOGY. I say this as a person who read the original 3 foundation novels before anything else. I decided to read everything in the "chronological" order. If I had not already read the original trilogy, Forward The Foundation would have spoiled everything for me!!! This is a book that is clearly written as a prequel, that is meant to be read AFTER the foundation trilogy, not before. <br/><br/>Onto the actual review. I loved this book. It fill</span>
  <span id="freeText1800928112150898618" style="display:none">Let me start out by saying DO NOT READ THIS BEFORE THE ORIGINAL TRILOGY. I say this as a person who read the original 3 foundation novels before anything else. I decided to read everything in the "chronological" order. If I had not already read the original trilogy, Forward The Foundation would have spoiled everything for me!!! This is a book that is clearly written as a prequel, that is meant to be read AFTER the foundation trilogy, not before. <br /><br />Onto the actual review. I loved this book. It filled in so much interesting history. It basically explains the whole road toward psychohistory and what leads up to the original trilogy. It's a great book to read afterwards, because it gives you all the background on how the galactic empire got to where it did. This book spans the life of Seldon from his 30s until his 80s. It's basically broken up into a decade at a time, give or take. You skip ahead a decade after each major plot twist. It's really well done as well. I was expecting this book to be a bore. People complain about it being boring a lot, and about it being unessential reading, and that we could easily skip it. I would say, this is ESSENTIAL READING. This book fills in so much stuff, it's quite impressive! Having read the whole series, I can see how this book shows what's to come, as well as what already came to pass. But you won't have a clue until you finish the very last sequel.<br /><br />I really should give this 5 stars. In a way, Prelude to Foundation, which I gave 4 stars, was more engaging. It was fast paced. Exciting. This was exciting but not in as much of an action packed way, which I'm perfectly happy with. This book had some impressively emotional moments in it as well! <br /><br />If you want to read foundation, read it all in publication order. I must stress that. For a first reading at least. If you wish to read chronologically, do so after having already read it in original publication order. You can skip the empire novels and read those later (read them, but maybe wait till you finish everything else first).<br /><br />Don't listen to the people saying this book isn't good. I've read a lot of science fiction, and not a single one of asimovs books I've read displeased me in the slightest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1800928112150898618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1037976930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1037976930" />
    <a title="Ken Doggett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26895953-ken-doggett"><img alt="Ken Doggett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475147230p2/26895953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1037976930?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken Doggett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken Doggett" href="/user/show/26895953-ken-doggett">Ken Doggett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385247931" href="/book/show/415995.Forward_the_Foundation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1037976930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14310779140010842530">I've always loved the clarity and humor of Asimov's science articles, but I've never been a fan of his fiction, and this book points up why. The characters are cardboard throughout, and any human behavior he gives them seems contrived and thrown in as it occurs to the author that something is needed. Asimov never places you into the scene, and the reader is left watching from afar.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76679.Forward_the_Foundation__Foundation_Prequel___2_' title='Forward the Foundation (Foundation Prequel, #2) by Isaac Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Forward the Foundation</a> is the second prequel to his famous Foundation series, and it was written shortly before his </span>
  <span id="freeText14310779140010842530" style="display:none">I've always loved the clarity and humor of Asimov's science articles, but I've never been a fan of his fiction, and this book points up why. The characters are cardboard throughout, and any human behavior he gives them seems contrived and thrown in as it occurs to the author that something is needed. Asimov never places you into the scene, and the reader is left watching from afar.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76679.Forward_the_Foundation__Foundation_Prequel___2_" title="Forward the Foundation (Foundation Prequel, #2) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Forward the Foundation</a> is the second prequel to his famous Foundation series, and it was written shortly before his death. It provides the finishing touches on the life of his fictional psychohistorian, Hari Seldon, and makes several revelations about certain characters, such as his wife Dors, that are only hinted at in the first. This one isn't as good as the first prequel, which itself had some of the same problems I found here. This one has a hurried feel to it, almost as if Asimov knew that his time was drawing to an end, and he wanted it finished at all costs. He died of a heart attack and kidney failure, so he might also been in poor health during the writing of this book, and couldn't exert as much effort on it as he would have liked. However, with all that said, it was brilliantly plotted, and the ending was touching. Other places in the book excelled as well, but overall I was happy to get to the ending.<br /><br />I intend next to reread Foundation. I read it so many years ago that I remember nothing about it, and all I can say for today is that reading it obviously didn't convert me into a fan of Asimov's fiction. I'll try it again.<br /><br />I do not recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76679.Forward_the_Foundation__Foundation_Prequel___2_" title="Forward the Foundation (Foundation Prequel, #2) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Forward the Foundation</a> to any but the most diehard of Asimov's fans (who may be more delighted with it than I was), and although I hesitate, I have to rate this one at only two out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14310779140010842530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_57314754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57314754" />
    <a title="Steven Peterson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1677868-steven-peterson"><img alt="Steven Peterson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442471489p2/1677868.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57314754?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven Peterson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven Peterson" href="/user/show/1677868-steven-peterson">Steven Peterson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57314754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4973831151269147301">In terms of Asimov's writing, this is the last work exploring the Foundation; the copyright date is actually after his death. As some have noted, there is something of a contradiction here. By the time the Foundation series ends (with "Foundation and Earth"), the Foundation is kaput in terms of the future, and Galaxia is to take its place. So, to make his last novel a Hari Seldon novel is a bit strange. Still and all, though, this is a fascinating novel.<br/><br/>There are a couple other books that link t</span>
  <span id="freeText4973831151269147301" style="display:none">In terms of Asimov's writing, this is the last work exploring the Foundation; the copyright date is actually after his death. As some have noted, there is something of a contradiction here. By the time the Foundation series ends (with "Foundation and Earth"), the Foundation is kaput in terms of the future, and Galaxia is to take its place. So, to make his last novel a Hari Seldon novel is a bit strange. Still and all, though, this is a fascinating novel.<br /><br />There are a couple other books that link the Robot series with the Foundation series. In some senses, this represents the apogee of that linkage, as we see in the first part of the novel, "Eto Semerzel." This character is a top advisor to King Cleon I, one of the last competent royals of the already declining Empire. And, oh boy, what a link is revealed in this segment to the Robot series.<br /><br />There are three other main episodes, one focusing on Cleon himself; one is entitled "Dors Venabili"; the final part is "Wanda Seldon." Then, a very brief segment representing Hari Seldon's last moments. The varying parts of this novel are not seamlessly welded together. However, by the end of his career, Asimov was capable of creating characters (compare with the essentially lifeless, cardboard figures of the original Foundation trilogy). As a result, this work is fascinating in that it is also an index of Asimov's growth as a writer. He went from an academic teaching Chemistry (if memory serves) to a pretty skilled author.<br /><br />Anyhow, the work is not tightly pulled together, but it is fascinating in its character development, its place in the Foundation series, its linking of the Robot series to the Foundation series. Surely not the best of the Foundation series, but one of the most intriguing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4973831151269147301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81195216?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Max Anadon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Max Anadon" href="/user/show/1595702-max-anadon">Max Anadon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81195216" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9212031227734342249">This is actually the second prequel to the Foundation Trilogy, and the last book Asimov wrote (see the Author's note in Prelude to Foundation for the chronology of the series vs. when actually penned).<br/><br/>As I read 'Prelude' first, and got accustomed to the later writing style of Asimov before getting to the Foundation Trilogy, it was easy for me to rejoin Hari, Dors, and Raych. The book is separated in sections by character focus, similar to others of the series. Each section jumps forward in time,</span>
  <span id="freeText9212031227734342249" style="display:none">This is actually the second prequel to the Foundation Trilogy, and the last book Asimov wrote (see the Author's note in Prelude to Foundation for the chronology of the series vs. when actually penned).<br /><br />As I read 'Prelude' first, and got accustomed to the later writing style of Asimov before getting to the Foundation Trilogy, it was easy for me to rejoin Hari, Dors, and Raych. The book is separated in sections by character focus, similar to others of the series. Each section jumps forward in time, and it is one of the things I appreciate about Asimov...the way he will jump ahead and lead you into the new section (although sometimes I didn't want the gaps in time...I wanted more details, more of what happened with the fallout of the resolution of the previous section). <br /><br />Hari ages through the book, and loses loved ones in the process. I felt the loss, and didn't want it to happen (especially Dors), but the additional emotion made it more enjoyable for me. A continued practice was the notes from the Galactic Encyclopedia at different parts of the book...I always liked those...<br /><br />Lots of gaps are filled, and it makes it very satisfying for a fan of the series...and even as a prequel, I didn't feel cheated by reading the rest of the series and coming back to this one. The last section jumped a bit back and forth with the time aspect, and I felt it lost the flow just a bit, but not so as to distract from the overall entertainment. <br /><br />I've got Foundation and Earth left to read, and then I'll go on to the robot series...certain to read the history of Daneel...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9212031227734342249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_375874337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/375874337" />
    <a title="Scott Rhee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5717792-scott-rhee"><img alt="Scott Rhee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408223108p2/5717792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/375874337?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott Rhee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott Rhee" href="/user/show/5717792-scott-rhee">Scott Rhee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5717792-scott-rhee?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer375874337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7403835237443587982">Isaac Asimov's "Foundation" series is considered to be one of the best sci-fi series ever written. That is perhaps a matter of personal opinion, but it is clear that Asimov has staying power based on the popularity of his books, roughly sixty years after many of them were published. "Forward the Foundation" is actually, in terms of the storyline's chronology, the second book in the series, a sequel to "Prelude to Foundation" and the book leading in to "Foundation", but it was actually the most r</span>
  <span id="freeText7403835237443587982" style="display:none">Isaac Asimov's "Foundation" series is considered to be one of the best sci-fi series ever written. That is perhaps a matter of personal opinion, but it is clear that Asimov has staying power based on the popularity of his books, roughly sixty years after many of them were published. "Forward the Foundation" is actually, in terms of the storyline's chronology, the second book in the series, a sequel to "Prelude to Foundation" and the book leading in to "Foundation", but it was actually the most recently written and published, just a year before his death in 1992. Like "Prelude", it is a fun, thoughtful science fiction/adventure yarn that carries on the story of Hari Seldon and his development of psychohistory and the two Foundations. His wife, Dors Venabili, adopted son Raych, and grand-daughter Wanda all play integral roles in the novel. What makes the novel more than just a fun yarn, though, is the deeply moving almost semi-autobiographical thread that runs through the novel: Hari Seldon is clearly, in this story, an idealized version of Asimov, who, writing this novel in the twilight of his life and only a year before his passing, was more than likely re-examining the life he had led. Seldon/Asimov's Foundation is his legacy, a chance to live on beyond death and to contribute to a better and brighter future for his children and ours. Time will tell, but I believe that Asimov's wonderful and prolific oeuvre of thoughtful fiction and nonfiction has already succeeded in helping to create a better future.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7403835237443587982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_435879259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/435879259" />
    <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse"><img alt="Ms. Smartarse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401273675p2/13703358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/435879259?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4249228416855066674">"The Domestic Life of Hari Seldon." <br/><br/>The last Foundation book Asimov wrote (1993) is the also the one right before the original trilogy begins (1951). Like the earlier 'prequel' novel, this book just kind of meanders without much of a central conflict or plot.   <span id="freeText4249228416855066674" style="display:none">"The Domestic Life of Hari Seldon." <br /><br />The last Foundation book Asimov wrote (1993) is the also the one right before the original trilogy begins (1951). Like the earlier 'prequel' novel, this book just kind of meanders without much of a central conflict or plot. There are some tie-ins to other Foundation works or his other series, but ultimately, but book just kind of plods along. The character dynamics (never Asimov's strong suit) are particularly unsatisfying as there isn't enough external stimuli to keep them interesting.<br /><br />A good chunk of the book is Seldon as crotchety First Minister, Seldon as crotchety psychohistorian, Seldon as crotchety septuagenarian. The major 'plot' of Seldon trying to get his adopted son to infiltrate a rebellious political faction never delivers and the various narrative payoffs are neither revelatory or interesting. </span>

<div id="review_1053369292" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1053369292" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/291872-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255380005p2/291872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1053369292?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/291872-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=sequel">sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1053369292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4184316104680155344">And with this volume, I bring to a close the Foundation series by Asimov (sort of; I'm still planning on reading the Benford-Bear-Brin books, since those at least have a pretty devoted following, too). I'm partly glad to be finished, since the stories tended to be somewhat repetitious and lacking in vivid characterization, but after all that Asimov did with the series and how he pulled it together with his other major science fiction novels, part of me wonders where he would have gone with it ha</span>
  <span id="freeText4184316104680155344" style="display:none">And with this volume, I bring to a close the Foundation series by Asimov (sort of; I'm still planning on reading the Benford-Bear-Brin books, since those at least have a pretty devoted following, too). I'm partly glad to be finished, since the stories tended to be somewhat repetitious and lacking in vivid characterization, but after all that Asimov did with the series and how he pulled it together with his other major science fiction novels, part of me wonders where he would have gone with it had he had more time to develop his ideas. Because as I mentioned in the last five reviews, his ideas take precedence over the storytelling.<br /><br />I also found this volume to be a bit of a throwback to the first book, in that instead of it being one singular story, the novel was comprised of four distinctive shorter works that told a larger story. Each story is about Hari Seldon and his days following his end as First Minister, from his early forties to his death some forty years later. We see more of the conflicts Seldon endured, politically and personally, and while it doesn't necessarily further the idea of Foundation, we get more insight into Seldon as a person, which was far more than what we received in Foundation. But the structure of the novel into its smaller parts brought the series full circle.<br /><br />So much of the story was about Seldon working on psychohistory without telling anyone save for his closest contacts that he was working on psychohistory, and that part of the story was a little tedious. The series overall had a lot of repetition in theme, structure, and narrative (each book seemed to review much of what came before, which, while necessary, was somewhat annoying when reading the stories all as one), and I wished that Asimov had tried giving his readers the benefit of the doubt at some point. The use of Dors and Rayche as a means to go into great length about the details of psychohistory also felt somewhat overused (even if it was necessary).<br /><br />I enjoyed the series well enough overall, and I can see why it has the reputation it does, but when it comes to sheer storytelling, it doesn't measure up. Characterization takes a back seat to the technical details, and without that connection to the characters, it was hard for me to care much about what happened to Hari and his family. The emotional scenes felt flat, leaving me mostly unresponsive, and I found myself reading to see where Asimov was taking the ideas instead of reading to see what would happen to the characters. That just doesn't seem like the right approach to take when writing fiction.<br /><br />Would I still recommend it? Yes. I'm not sure if I would recommend reading them all at once, as I did, but some time away from the series might make some of that repetition less grating. As it is, I'm looking forward to seeing what other authors have to do with the characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4184316104680155344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer609429570530471832">The unfinished glimpse of Seldon building the foundation of The Foundation at the end of the Galactic Empire left me intrigued about Seldon and the history of Psychohistory. <br/><br/>The first glimpse of Seldon and the unrest at the Galactic Capital Trantor was written by Asimov at the age of twenty-one (how sad that I've written nothing of significance at even a decade older than that)! Undoubtedly the same intrugueness was felt by thousands of other readers of Asimov, or he would have never written the</span>
  <span id="freeText609429570530471832" style="display:none">The unfinished glimpse of Seldon building the foundation of The Foundation at the end of the Galactic Empire left me intrigued about Seldon and the history of Psychohistory. <br /><br />The first glimpse of Seldon and the unrest at the Galactic Capital Trantor was written by Asimov at the age of twenty-one (how sad that I've written nothing of significance at even a decade older than that)! Undoubtedly the same intrugueness was felt by thousands of other readers of Asimov, or he would have never written the history of the 'Historian' of the Future. <br /><br />While Prelude To Foundation was filled with surprises, especially near the end, as is customary of the Foundation series and sort of a trend with Asimov, Forward has been rather linear, a straightforward narration of the decades in Seldon and Psychohistory. <br /><br />It was wonderful to read. I am glad to begin the year with such a good read. The storyline remains complex and simple at the same time, including the values of humanity as well as the struggle of academics, the funding of a project, the politics of a world. <br /><br />Although this was written as the very last book of the series, I wanted to read and know how Seldon the scientist ends his career as the new Foundation begins, before I proceeded with the interludes. <br /><br />Foundation the book series is much like Star Wars the movie series in many ways.. ways where the millions of worlds of Galactic Empires come together. They also are very different of course. But they both begin in the middle, look back and then jump forward again. It was a pleasure to see the new Star Wars just before reading this book. May life be as fulfilling always when it comes to entertainmemt. :)</span>

<div id="review_3492235337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3492235337" />
    <a title="Frederik Raud" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44078590-frederik-raud"><img alt="Frederik Raud" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560979248p2/44078590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3492235337?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frederik Raud" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frederik Raud" href="/user/show/44078590-frederik-raud">Frederik Raud</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18138897-forward-the-foundation">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3492235337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15524618067159045575">The last book in the <i>Foundation</i> series stands out for being unusually weak.<br/><br/>Asimov’s plotting has always been that of a pulpy adventure writer and his characters have always been shallow. Usually this is balanced out by either well-written drama, interesting science fiction concepts, or in the case of the <i>Foundation</i> series, the unusual birds-eye-view portrayal of history and the concept of predestination.<br/><br/><i>Forward the Foundation</i> has none of these redeeming qualities. The writing is punchy but the d</span>
  <span id="freeText15524618067159045575" style="display:none">The last book in the <i>Foundation</i> series stands out for being unusually weak.<br /><br />Asimov’s plotting has always been that of a pulpy adventure writer and his characters have always been shallow. Usually this is balanced out by either well-written drama, interesting science fiction concepts, or in the case of the <i>Foundation</i> series, the unusual birds-eye-view portrayal of history and the concept of predestination.<br /><br /><i>Forward the Foundation</i> has none of these redeeming qualities. The writing is punchy but the dialogue is more awkward than ever. The political drama of the book is undermined by its shallow takes and its moustache-twirling villains. This would be acceptable if it didn’t make up over half of the book. And I doubt Asimov was being paid by the word. It lacks any of the inventiveness we've come to expect from him, there are no new themes or science fiction elements. In the sequels Asimov dealt with the contradictions of the individual and the community and did so on a cosmical scale. In <i>Forward the Foundation</i> the community has won out completely. This calcification of beliefs and lack of curiosity is what leads the work's political bits to lose any semblance of drama. The tenets that ‘the ends justify the means’ and that ‘the needs of the many outweigh the needs of the few’ do simplify the human equation indeed.<br /><br /><b>Spoilers:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The book introduces one new meaningful character: Wanda, Seldon’s granddaughter on whose shoulders rests the future of the Seldon plan and thus humanity. Everyone besides her, Seldon, and perhaps Yugo Amaryl are there just to make the plot happen and even if they have one or more dimensions they have already reached the end of their character arcs by the start of this book.<br /> The series suffers from sequel syndrome. Asimov stops developing new characters. The old ones are recycled and assigned new roles to fulfil. As the number of books in the series reaches infinity, everybody becomes ‘Actually’ Daneel Olivaw.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The read was a bore and for most of it I considered giving the book two stars and I’m usually very easy to please and am able to ignore authorial wankery and weirdness if the work at least gives me something. The third star I award for the epilogue, which was well supported by the previous chapters. It’s also a satisfying conclusion to the series as a whole. But in no way does it justify the rest of this trite and unless you’re a super fan or a completionist, I do not recommend reading the prequels.<br /><br />As I compiled my thoughts for this review, I arrived at the belief that <i>Forward the Foundation</i> would have been a much better book, were it written entirely from Wanda’s point of view. I feel like Asimov was going for something akin to the multi-generational plot of <i>One Hundred Years of Solitude</i> but failed to replicate anything that was good about it. Also, I have no fucking clue how the Apple TV+ adaptation is going to do anything with the story and the trailer makes it even more puzzling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15524618067159045575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
